1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# End-to-End: How Kubernetes Creates a Deployment

## Your Task

You are onboarding to the Kubernetes project. A senior engineer has asked you to produce
a technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created — tracing the full
request flow from a client application through the API server and into persistent storage.

**Your question**: Explain how a Kubernetes client application creates a Deployment from
start to finish. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Client library** — What type/function in `kubernetes-client-go` sends the HTTP request?
2. **API server** — What function in `kubernetes/kubernetes` receives and validates the create request?
3. **Storage** — What function in `etcd-io/etcd` persists the Deployment to the key-value store?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/type name.

## Context

You are working in a Kubernetes ecosystem with the following repos:

- `kubernetes/kubernetes` (the core orchestrator)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (go-client-library)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-api` (api-type-definitions)
- `etcd-io/etcd` (distributed-kv-store)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. Use your
search tools to trace the full path across repositories.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.go",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrTypeName",
      "description": "What this step does in the flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining the end-to-end flow, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use exact repo identifiers as they appear in Sourcegraph. The oracle expects `repo` values of `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (client layer), `kubernetes/kubernetes` (API server layer), and `etcd-io/etcd` (storage layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (client → server → storage)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers clearly?

## Summary

The answer is saved in `/workspace/answer.json` and traces the complete flow across all three repositories:

### **Client Layer** (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)
- **File**: `gentype/type.go`
- **Function**: `Client[T].Create()` (line 244)
- **What it does**: Sends an HTTP POST request with the Deployment object serialized in the body

### **API Server Layer** (kubernetes/kubernetes)
- **File**: `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go`
- **Function**: `NewREST()` (line 73)
- **What it does**: Creates the REST handler that receives the create request, validates the Deployment using deployment strategy, and delegates to the generic registry store

### **Storage Layer** (etcd-io/etcd)
- **File**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go`
- **Function**: `kvServer.Put()` (line 55)
- **What it does**: Receives the gRPC Put request and persists the Deployment key-value pair to etcd's distributed storage using Raft consensus

The answer includes detailed explanations of how each layer processes the request, from client-side HTTP construction through API server validation to final persistence in the etcd key-value store.

Client Library Layer (kubernetes-client-go)\\n\\nThe process begins in the client library at `gentype/type.go:244`. When a user calls `deploymentsClient.Create(ctx, deployment, metav1.CreateOptions{})`, this invokes the `Client[T].Create()` method (where T is *appsv1.Deployment). This method constructs an HTTP POST request by:\\n- Calling `c.client.Post()` to initiate a POST request builder\\n- Setting the resource path via `.Resource(\\\"deployments\\\")`\\n- Adding the Deployment object as the request body via `.Body(obj)`\\n- Executing the request with `.Do(ctx)`\\n\\nThe client sends the serialized Deployment object to the API server endpoint (typically `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments`).\\n\\n## 2. API Server Layer (kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\nThe API server receives the request and routes it to the Deployment REST handler, initialized in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go` via the `NewREST()` function. This function creates a `REST` struct that embeds `*genericregistry.Store` (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`).\\n\\nThe REST handler:\\n1. Validates the incoming Deployment object using the `deploymentStrategy.PrepareForCreate()` method\\n2. Applies any necessary field defaults (e.g., setting `Generation: 1`)\\n3. Delegates the actual persistence to the `genericregistry.Store.Create()` method\\n4. The Store interface validates the object and applies admission webhooks/policies\\n\\nThe Store then constructs an etcd key path (typically `/registry/deployments/{namespace}/{name}`) and calls the storage backend.\\n\\n## 3. Storage Layer (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\nThe API server's storage layer communicates with etcd via the gRPC protocol. The etcd server receives the request at the `kvServer.Put()` method in `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go:55`.\\n\\nThis method:\\n1. Validates the PutRequest to ensure the key and value are properly formed\\n2. Calls `s.kv.Put(ctx, r)` where `s.kv` is a `RaftKV` interface that manages the distributed consensus\\n3. The request is logged in the etcd Raft log and replicated across the cluster\\n4. Once the write is committed, the Deployment is persisted in etcd's internal MVCC (Multi-Version Concurrency Control) storage\\n5. Returns a PutResponse containing the revision number of the write\\n\\nThe revision number is then propagated back through the API server to the client, confirming successful creation.\\n\\n## Complete Request Path Summary\\n\\n1. **Client**: `gentype/type.go:Client.Create()` \u2192 HTTP POST request\\n2. **API Server**: `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go:NewREST()` \u2192 REST handler + validation\\n3. **Generic Registry**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:Store.Create()` \u2192 Storage abstraction\\n4. **etcd Storage**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go:kvServer.Put()` \u2192 Persistent storage in distributed KV store\\n\\nThis three-layer architecture ensures that Deployments are validated, authorized, and reliably persisted across the Kubernetes cluster.\"\n}\n",

Returns a PutResponse containing the revision number of the write\\n\\nThe revision number is then propagated back through the API server to the client, confirming successful creation.\\n\\n## Complete Request Path Summary\\n\\n1. **Client**: `gentype/type.go:Client.Create()` \u2192 HTTP POST request\\n2. **API Server**: `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go:NewREST()` \u2192 REST handler + validation\\n3. **Generic Registry**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:Store.Create()` \u2192 Storage abstraction\\n4. **etcd Storage**: `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/key.go:kvServer.Put()` \u2192 Persistent storage in distributed KV store\\n\\nThis three-layer architecture ensures that Deployments are validated, authorized, and reliably persisted across the Kubernetes cluster.\"\n}\n",
